insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('budon','budo(n.)','A term denoting the way of the warnor during the early-modern period, from the modern period it refers to learning how to live as a human being through training； in the martial arts. In 1919 (Taisho 8), the Dai-Nippon Butokukai, the supervising organization for the martial arts at that time, changed the names of gekken, jujutsu, and kyujutsu to kendo, juao, and kyudo, respectively. The term budo was then used to refer collectively to these disciplines. The new names reflected the fact that martial arts training has an important spirtual side, and does not consist only of training in techniques, Today, budo encompasses even more disciplines, with the term being used widely to refer to martial arts such as kendo, judo, kyudo, sumo，naginata, aikido, karatedd, jukendo, and shorinji kenpo. See bushido.','EN','b','',1);

The dan system was originally adopted in Kodo-kan Judo, with the first shodan being issued in 1883 (Meiji 16). The kyu system was used in kendo mainly by the Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department and was systematized in 1885 (Meiji 18). In kendo, the Tokyo Higher Normal School first used dan in 1908 (Meiji 41). Depending on how one uses one''s mind, however, it can also become a skill to enhance one''s own life, and that of the opponent too (katsunin-ken). A swing of the sword gives the practitioner a chance to become aware of life and death, both one''s own and others''. This is a central tenet of modern kendo. One lives one''s life only once, and that life depends on each swing of the sword (shinai). As such, one should commit body and soul into every swing. Consequently, in order to perfect the swing, ken- no-riho (the principles of the sword) guide the way in striving to execute the proper striking techniques smoothly, and with the proper mental attitude, posture and full spirit. insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('mittsunosenn','三つの先（せん）','剣道においては機先を制することが最も重要である。「先」の取り合いが勝負を決定するともいえる。「先」には「三つの先」があるといわれている。高野佐三郎の『剣道』では「三つの先」を「先々（せんせん）の先」「先」「後の先」として解説している。それらを要約すると次のようになる。先々の先：相手と相対し勝敗を争うとき、相手の起こりをいちはやく機微の間に認めて、直ちに打ち込み、機先を制することをいう。相手の「先」より更にその先（さき）をゆくことで、剣道において最も重要なことで ある。懸りの先ともいう。先：隙を認めて相手が打ち込んで来るのを、相手の先が効を奏する前に早く先を取って勝つことをいう。対（たい）の先ともいう。後の先：隙を認めて相手が打ち込んでくるのを、切り落としたり、太刀を凌いだりした後に、相手の気勢が萎えた所を強く打ち込んで勝つことをいう。待（たい）の先ともいう。','JA','m','',1);
insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('mittsunosenn','mittsu-no-sen (n.)','The three sen. in Kendo it is of paramount importance to suppress the opponent''s move at the moment it begins. It could be said that the competition to take sen decides the match. There are three sen (mittsu-no-sen). In the book titled Kendo written by Takano Sasaburo, the mittsu-no-sen are explained as sensen-no-sen, sen, and go-no-sen. These three can be summarized as follows:sensen-no-sen: When facing an opponent in a match, having the keen insight to quickly recognize the opponent''s start，and then attack immediately，,thus forestalling the opponent''s move.This act of attacking faster than the opponent''s sen is the most important in kendo. Also called kakari-no-sen. sen: When the opponent sees a suki (weakness) in your defenses and initiates an attack, winning by striking in turn before the opponent''s strike is successful. Also called tai- no-sen.go-no-sen: When the opponent sees a suki (weakness) and initiates an attack, winning by first striking down the opponent''s sword or parrying, then attacking strongly when the opponent has become discouraged. Also called tai-no-sen.','EN','m','',1);

insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('reihon','reiho (n.)','Courtesy. In kendo there is ritsurei and za- rei. Ritsurei is a bow performed while standing. It is the standard courtesy shown at the beginning and the end of kendo matches and keiko. Ritsurei in the shomen direction is performed at an angle of 30 degrees. Ritsurei to each other in matches and keiko is done at an angle of 15 degrees. Zarei is a bow from the formal kneeling position. It is performed as follows: 1 Watch the opponent. 2 Lean the upper-body forward while simultaneously putting both hands on the floor and bowing slowly. 3 After pausing in this position for a moment (about one breath), return to the original position (seiza) and watch the opponent. The hands should be placed as shown in theillustrations. The point of the nose should be mthe direction of the asterisk in the picture. ','EN','r','',1);

insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('shiaihohon','shiai-hoho (n.)','The format of a match. Kojin-shiai and dantai- shiai are two of the types used. A kojin-shiai is an individual match (individual vs. individual), and a dantai-shiai is a team match (team vs. team). A team is made up of three, five, or seven members. Other types include rigu-sen (a league match) and tonamento-sen (a tournament match). In rigu-sen a group of individuals or teams do a round robin, ana overall victory is decided based on the winning percentage. In to namento-sen winners continue to fight, and the last remaining winner gets the first prize. There are two methods used for team matches: the shoshasu-ho, and the kachinuki-ho. In the shoshasu-ho, the winning team is decided by the total number of individual wins. In the kachitnuki-ho, beginning with the first player from each team (the senpo) the matches continue with the victor facing the players of the opposing team, one after another, until he or she is defeated. Finally, the team with the last survivor wins.','EN','s','',1);

insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('shinaikyogin','shinai-kyogi (n.)','After World War II, kendo was prohibited by GHQ (General Headquarters). In 1950 (Showa 25) the All Japan Shinai Kyogi Federation was founded and kendo was remodeled into shinai- kyogi, a kind of competitive sport, which became the basis for the revival of traditional kendo. A fukuro-shinai (two thirds of the length of bamboo was split into four, eight, sixteen, and more pieces, and covered with a cloth bag) was used, and the players wore long-sleeved shirts and pants, and used equipment which originated in European fencing. Rules and refereeing methods were defined, and competitions held in which the winner was decided based on the number of points scored in a given time. In 1954 (Showa 29), the federation was combined with the All Japan Kendo Federation, so shinai-kyogi was unified with kendo and disappeared as a matter of course.','EN','s','',1);

insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('shinkiryokuitchin','shin-ki-ryoku-itchi (n.)','A phrase which expresses the essential point one should keep in mind when engaging in offence and defence. Shin-ki-ryoku-itchi is the teaching that when one intuitively perceives a stimulus from the opponent, all three elements of shin (mind), ki (outward action based upon the judgement of the mind) and ryoku (action) must be expressed instantaneously in the form of a waza. Shin refers to the mind or the calm part of one''s mental functions, and it is the ability to intuitively sense the opponent''s condition and movements，and to make judgements. Ki appears as an outward action based upon the judgement of the mind (shin), and is the dynamic part of one''s mental function. Ryoku refers to the action of the body or of a waza.','EN','s','',1);

insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('sonkyon','sonkyo (n.)','Originally a protocol of thecourtesy done with one''s knees bent to show respect. In kendo, it is a squatting posture balancing on one'' s toes with the right foot slightly forward, the buttocks lowered, the knees opened outward, and the upper-body upright. At the beginning of a match or practice, this serves as a preparatory posture in which one can prepare and adjust one''s spirit vis-a-vis the opponent, decide what maai to maintain, and determine how to carry one''s self. Also, at the end of a match or practice, this posture requires a full spirit, and ends in a dignified manner. When performing Nippon Kendo Kata, the uchidachi waits in the sonkyo posture when the shidachi changes an odachi for a kodachi. In a match, competitors wait in this position while the opponent is rearranging his or her chakuso.','EN','s','',1);

Generally speaking, alter striking one should put the proper distance between one''s self and the opponent, and face him or her in the chudan posture ready for a possible counterattack. If one cannot move the proper distance, place the tip of the shinai in the center or around the throat of the opponent to guard against a counterattack. According to the Regulations and Subsidiary Rules of Kendo Shiai and Shinpan, zanshin is one of the conditions for yuko-datotsu. Therefore, if one does not show good body posture and state of mind with respect to the opponent after striking, a yuko-datotsu	may be cancelled. insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('kinshikoijikon','禁止行為事項','禁止行為とは試合中にしてはいけない次の事項の行為で、罰則が適用される。①禁止されている薬物を使用または保持すること。②審判員または相手に対し、非礼な言動をすること。上記①、②に対しての罰則は最も厳しく、この行為を犯した者は負けとし、相手に2本を与え、退場を命ぜられる。退場させられた者の既得本数および既得権は認められない。③定められた以外の用具(不正用具）を使用すること。不正用具の使用者は負けとし、相手に2本を与え、既得本数および既得権は認められない。ただし、不正用具の使用が発覚した以前の試合までさかのぼらないこととなっている。 不正用具の使用が発覚した者は、その後の試合を継続することはできないが、団体戦における補欠の出場は別に定めのない限り認められる。また、両者が同時に不正用具を使用した場合は両者とも負けとし、それぞれの既得本数および既得権は認められない。④相手に足をかけまたは払うこと。⑤相手を不当に場外に出すこと。⑥試合中に場外に出ること。⑦自己の竹刀を落とすこと。⑧不当な中止を要請すること。⑨その他、試合規則に反する次のような行為をすること。•相手に手をかけまたは抱え込むこと。•相手の竹刀を握るまたは自分の竹刀の刃部を握ること。•相手の竹刀を抱えること。•相手の肩に故意に竹刀をかけること。•倒れたとき、相手の攻撃に対応することなく、うつ伏せなどになること。•故意に時間を空費すること。•不当な鍔ぜり合いおよび不当な打突をすること。④~⑨までの行為に対する罰則は反則とし、2回犯した場合は相手に1本を与える。反則は1試合を通じて積算される。ただし、同時反則によって両者が負けになる場合は相殺し反則としない。⑥については、両者が相前後して場外に出たときは先に出た者のみを反則とする。また、有効打突を取り消したときは反則としない。⑦については、竹刀を落とした直後に相手が打突を加え、有効となっ たときは反則としない。','JA','k','',1);
insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('kinshikoijikon','kinshi-koi-jiko (n.)','The term kinshi-koi refers to the following prohibited acts which are penalized during a match.①The use or possession of prohibited drugs. ②Insulting or acting offensively toward a referee or the opponent. The penalties for 1 and 2 are the most severe, and someone who breaks these rules will lose the match and be ordered to retire from the match court; the opponent shall be given two points. The points and status the violator already acquired are nullified.③Use of kendo equipment other than that stipulated.Someone who uses prohibited equipment shall lose the match, and the opponent shall be given two points. The points and status gained by the violator shall be nullified, but this nullification shall not be retroactive to preceding matches in which the use of the prohibited kendo equipment was not detected. Someone wno is detected using prohibited equipment shall be disallowed from participating in the remaining matches, but the violator may be substituted in a team match unless otherwise stipulated.When both players use prohibited equipment, both shall lose the match, and the points and status of both wil be nullified. ④Tripping or sweeping the opponent''s leg(s). ⑤Unfairly shoving or pushing an opponent out of the match court. ⑥Stepping out of the match court.⑦Dropping the shinai.⑧Requesting suspension of the match without a justifiable reason.⑨Committing other acts that violate the Regulations Putting one''s hand on the opponent or holding the opponent in one''s arms. Taking hold of the opponent''s shinai or grasping one''s own shinai on its jinbu.Taking hold of the opponent''s shinai under one''s arm.Intentionally putting one''s shinai on the opponent''s shoulder.Lying face down after having fallen on the floor without responding to the opponent''s attack.Intentionally wasting time.Doing improper tsubazeriai or datotsu.The acts committed in (4) to (9) are regarded as hansoku, and when a player commits two such violations, the opponent shall be awarded one point. Violations shall be cumulative during the match. However, when both players commit a second violation and lose the match simultaneously, those violations shall be offset(sosai) and not result in a penalty. For 6, when both players have stepped out of The match court, only the person who first committed the violation will be subject to a penalty. When a yuko-datotsu (valid strike) is cancelled, the violation shall not be subject to a penalty.For 7，when the opponent makes a yuko-datot-su (valid strike) immediately after a player lets go of his or her own shinai, that violation shall not be subject to a penalty.','EN','k','',1);

When the match stops because of an injury or accident, the decision on whether or not the player can continue is made based on the overall judgement of the referees, taking into account a doctor''s opinion. With regard to the halting of a match when an injury or accident occurs, in principle, the referees should make the decision on whether the match can continue or not within five minutes. When such a situation arises, if the injury or accident was caused intentionally and was the fault of one side, the player who caused it loses the match, and his or her points and acquired status are invalidated. If the cause is not clear, the player who is unable to compete shall lose the match. The winner shall be given two points, but a single point already acquired by the loser will still be counted. In the case of an encho-sen(overtime match), the winner shall be given one point. insert into dicentries(code,title,content,language,initial,description,enable) values('yukodatotsun','yuko-datotsu (n.)','A valid strike which is considered ippon. According to the rules, a waza is complete when the following conditions are met: showing a fullness of spirit and appropriate posture, striking a datotsu-bui (striking zone) of the opponent with the striking region of the shinai while using correct hasuji, and expressing zanshin. If the necessary conditions are met, ippon is also given in the following cases: when one strikes the opponent as soon as he or she drops their shinai , steps out of the court, or falls down. Also when the opponent is struck just as the signal for the end of the match is given. Ippon is not given in the following cases: when both players simultaneously make valid strikes, and when one player makes a valid strike but the opponent shows full spirit and proper pos-ture and the tip of his or her shinai is planted firmly on the chest of the striking player. In the case of nito, yuko-datotsu with the shoto requires that the opponent''s daito be suppressed with the daito with the arm fully extended, and that the conditions for yuko-datotsu are fully met.','EN','y','',1);
